1	package fh.view.build
2	
3	import io.circe.Json
4	import io.circe.parser
5	import sjsonnet.{DefaultParseCache, Interpreter, OsPath, Settings, SjsonnetMainBase}
6	
7	/** In-process jsonnet evaluation for the build phase.
8	  *
9	  * Wraps sjsonnet so the dashboard `.jsonnet` (which imports
10	  * `components.libsonnet` and the generated `dump.libsonnet`) is evaluated to
11	  * JSON. This runs ONCE at build time — never on the runtime hot path.
12	  */
13	object JsonnetBuild {
14	
15	  /** Evaluation result: the JSON plus every file that was read to produce it
16	    * (the entry and its transitive imports), so callers can watch them.
17	    */
18	  case class Result(value: Json, imports: Set[os.Path])
19	
20	  /** Evaluate `entryFile` (relative to `dashboardsDir`), resolving imports from
21	    * that directory. Returns the evaluated JSON + import set, or an error
22	    * string.
23	    */
24	  def eval(
25	      dashboardsDir: os.Path,
26	      entryFile: String
27	  ): Either[String, Result] = {
28	    val entry = dashboardsDir / entryFile
29	    val importer = SjsonnetMainBase.SimpleImporter(Seq(OsPath(dashboardsDir)), None)
30	    // The parse cache is keyed by every parsed file, so after interpretation its
31	    // keys are the entry + all transitive imports.
32	    val cache = new DefaultParseCache
33	    val interpreter = new Interpreter(
34	      Map.empty[String, String], // ext vars: none — jsonnet is pure composition
35	      Map.empty[String, String], // top-level args: none
36	      OsPath(dashboardsDir),
37	      importer,
38	      cache,
39	      Settings.default
40	    )
41	
42	    interpreter
43	      .interpret(os.read(entry), OsPath(entry))
44	      .flatMap { ujsonValue =>
45	        parser.parse(ujsonValue.render()).left.map(_.message)
46	      }
47	      .map { json =>
48	        val imports =
49	          cache.keySet.iterator.collect { case (OsPath(p), _) =>
50	            p
51	          }.toSet + entry
52	        Result(json, imports)
53	... [1424 chars truncated]

1	// Dashboard components — pure composition (build phase only).
2	//
3	// Each component is defined in ONE place: a `_components` entry holding its
4	// Mustache `template`, the `slots` it declares (validated at build
5	// time), and its `build` function (the layout-tree node it emits). The
6	// backend-facing `cards` library is then DERIVED mechanically from those
7	// entries (see `cards` below), and the public builders are thin static fields
8	// delegating to each component's `build` — so a node references a card by name
9	// and supplies static values + slot references, never the template itself.
10	//
11	// Why a hidden `_components` + derived `cards` (rather than authoring `cards`
12	// directly): it co-locates each template with the builder that fills it (they
13	// must agree on input names), while keeping the builders as STATIC top-level
14	// fields — the only thing editors autocomplete. The derived `cards` map has
15	// dynamic keys (not autocompletable), but it is backend-facing only: authors
16	// call builders, never `c.cards.*`.
17	//
18	// Datastar v1 attribute syntax uses COLONS: `data-on:click`, `data-bind`,
19	// `data-signals`. A click is a whole Datastar expression carried by the
20	// `onclick` slot — a bare-string literal for a constant click (popup/navigate),
21	// or a `c.expr(...)` JSONata expression when it reads the entity per render:
22	//   - service call: @post('/sse/action/<domain>/<service>/<entity>')
23	//   - popup:        @post('/sse/surface/open|close/<id>')
24	//   - navigate:     @post('/sse/navigate/<slug>'); history.pushState(...)
25	// The slider's value-carrying change handler is assembled in its own template
26	// (it needs the per-instance signal `$val_{{id}}`):
27	//   @post('/sse/action/<domain>/<service>/<entity>/<key>/' + $signal)
28	//
29	// PHASE DISCIPLINE: templates never embed live values. Escaped `{{slot}}` values
30	// are HTML-safe; raw author values (action URLs, entity ids) use `{{{...}}}`.
31	// Literal t... [5481 chars truncated]

## pkl-core Java Embedding

The pkl-core library contains the Pkl parser, evaluator, REPL server, and Standard Library, and is the foundation for most of Pkl's other libraries and tools. The library can also be used to embed Pkl in Java libraries and applications.

The pkl-core library requires Java 17 or higher.

[tool result]
# Embedding pkl-core in Java Applications

## Core API and Evaluation

The `Evaluator` class provides the primary interface for embedding Pkl. According to the documentation, `"Evaluator is the core evaluator that exposes multiple methods of evaluation."` The main `evaluate()` method processes a module and returns a `PModule` object if successful, or throws `PklException` on failure.

For rendering evaluated modules, the library includes specialized visitors like `JsonRenderer`, `YamlRenderer`, `PcfRenderer`, and `PListRenderer`—allowing flexible output formatting beyond raw Java objects.

## JVM Requirements

The pkl-core library requires **Java 17 or higher**. The documentation makes no mention of GraalVM or Truffle interpreter requirements, suggesting it runs on standard JDK implementations.

## Security and Configuration

Two key customization areas exist:

1. **Security**: `"The (Pkl, not Java) security manager can be configured and customized using SecurityManagers and related classes."`

2. **Module Loading**: Module loaders support customization through `ModuleKeyFactories` and related abstractions, enabling control over how modules are resolved and loaded.

## Installation and Dependencies

The library is available from Maven Central. No details about dependency size or performance metrics are provided in this documentation excerpt.

The example code demonstrates straightforward usage: create an `Evaluator` via `preconfigured()`, evaluate a `ModuleSource`, then access the resulting `PModule` as Java objects.

ASSISTANT  2026-07-02T19:41:01.197Z
==============================================================================
The investigation is complete, including a working spike. Here's my assessment.

## Verdict: Pkl is a strong fit, and the Scala-side integration is small — the real cost is porting the 660-line component library

I read the current integration (`JsonnetBuild.scala`, `DashboardBuild.scala`, the jsonnet sources), researched Pkl's current state, and ran a hands-on spike: evaluated a Pkl module mimicking your dashboard model (typed nodes, typed entities, builder functions, comprehension + filter over a dump) from Scala via `org.pkl-lang:pkl-core:0.31.1`. Spike files are in `scratchpad/pkl-spike/` if you want to poke at them.

### Against your three requirements

**Compiler catches issues — yes, and it's the biggest win.** Pkl has classes, typed properties, nullability (`String?`, `??`), and constraint types (`entity_id: String(matches(Regex(...)))`). In the spike, an invalid entity id produced an error with carets pointing at *both* the constraint declaration and the violating value, with file:line. That makes two current mechanisms mostly obsolete: `Dashboard.validate`'s input checking (each card's declared `inputs` become typed class properties, checked at eval) and the grep-based `JsonnetBuild.literalLocator` hack, which exists precisely because jsonnet erases source positions. One honest limit: JSONata transform strings stay opaque strings to Pkl — those still need your runtime compile check.

**Editor autocomplete — yes, this is Pkl's differentiator over jsonnet.** Apple maintains an IntelliJ plugin, a VS Code extension, and pkl-lsp (Neovim too), with completion, go-to-definition, and type-aware diagnostics. Your `components.libsonnet` comment already laments that only static top-level fields autocomplete in jsonnet; in Pkl, card classes, their properties, and — if you codegen a typed dump — every floor/area/entity would complete. Caveat: pkl-lsp currently needs its own Java 22+ runtime (native executables are planned); the IntelliJ plugin doesn't have that constraint.

**Sharing — much stronger than jsonnet.** Pkl has a real package system: versioned packages published as GitHub release assets, imported via `import "package://..."` or as `PklProject` dependencies, with generated API docs (pkldoc). You could publish the card component library as a package that consumers import *with types and completion*, versus jsonnet's copy-the-libsonnet-file story.

### Integration difficulty

The Scala seam is exactly one function: `JsonnetBuild.eval` returns circe `Json` + an import set, and everything downstream (`normalizeChildren`, `hoistInlineSurfaces`, decode, validate, both phases) consumes JSON and doesn't care where it came from. Concrete facts from the spike:

- **Runs in-process on your stock OpenJDK 21** (needs 17+, no GraalVM). Single 3.3 MB jar — comparable to sjsonnet.
- `Evaluator.preconfigured().evaluateOutputText(...)` with a `JsonRenderer` output block gives JSON text → `io.circe.parser.parse` → existing pipeline unchanged. ~50 lines to write `PklBuild.eval`.
- **First eval 524 ms (classloading), warm re-eval ~0 ms** — fine for your startup-only/live-reload usage, never on the hot path.
- **Live-reload watch set**: sjsonnet's parse-cache trick has a direct replacement — Pkl 0.27+ ships an import-graph analysis API (`pkl:analyze` / the corresponding pkl-core API) that returns the transitive import set of an entry module.
- **The dump**: instead of writing `dump.libsonnet`, generate a *typed* `dump.pkl` (entities/areas/floors as class instances). This fits the project's whole codegen ethos and is what unlocks autocomplete on `dump.floors.overetasje.areas.bibliotek`. Straightforward string templating, same as your existing generators.
- Mustache `{{...}}` in templates doesn't collide with Pkl string syntax (interpolation is `\(...)`), and custom-delimiter strings (`#"..."#`) avoid escaping.

### The actual cost

Porting `components.libsonnet` (662 lines) plus theme/tokens and the six dashboards (~470 lines). Everything they use has a Pkl equivalent — local functions, lambdas, computed mapping keys, `for`/`when` generators in listings, `hidden` members — but the idioms differ meaningfully:

- **No named arguments on functions.** `c.button(action=..., label='« Home')` becomes either positional args or, more idiomatically, classes with amending: `new Button { action = navigate("dashboard"); label = "« Home" }`. The amending style is actually where the typing and completion come from, so leaning into it (rather than transliterating the builder functions) is the right port — but it's a redesign of the authoring surface, not a mechanical translation.
- Jsonnet's `obj + obj` merge patterns (e.g. `labelSlot` merging `c.expr(...)` descriptors) map to Pkl amending/spread, which behaves differently around defaults — the subtle parts of `components.libsonnet` need thought, not transliteration.

### Suggested path if you proceed

1. Keep `JsonnetBuild` and add `PklBuild` behind the same `Result` shape (they can coexist; entry-file extension picks the evaluator).
2. Codegen `dump.pkl` from `DataDump`.
3. Port the component library card-by-card as typed classes, moving each card's `inputs` contract into its class.
4. Port one small dashboard (`energy.jsonnet`, 27 lines) end-to-end to validate the model before committing to the rest.
5. Per your ADR convention, this supersedes parts of the "presentation is jsonnet composition" decision — the *composition-only, no-live-values* principle carries over unchanged, but the ADRs would need dated `## Update —` sections.

Sources: [pkl-core library docs](https://pkl-lang.org/main/current/pkl-core/index.html), [Java integration](https://pkl-lang.org/main/current/java-binding/index.html), [Pkl Language Server](https://pkl-lang.org/lsp/current/index.html), [IntelliJ plugin](https://pkl-lang.org/intellij/current/index.html), [Pkl 0.27 release notes (import analysis)](https://pkl-lang.org/main/current/release-notes/0.27.html), [pkl-pantry (shared packages)](https://github.com/apple/pkl-pantry), [publishing packages discussion](https://github.com/apple/pkl/discussions/668), [apple/pkl](https://github.com/apple/pkl).

ASSISTANT  2026-07-02T19:55:01.029Z

Yes to both — and I didn't just sketch it, I built and ran it. The full working spike is in `scratchpad/pkl-spike2/` (four `.pkl` files + a scala-cli runner using `pkl-core`), evaluated from Scala on your JDK 21, producing exactly the `{card, params, children}` JSON your pipeline already decodes. Here's how it looks.

## 1. The domain schema (`hass.pkl`) — hand-curated, one class per domain

This is the *shareable* module (it would ship as the Pkl package). One important design rule fell out naturally: the dump should contain only **capability** metadata (what an entity *can* do — from the HA entity docs), never live values. Live values (`state`, current `brightness`, current `hs_color`) stay runtime-side as JSONata over the SSE stream, which preserves your phase discipline exactly.

```pkl
typealias ColorMode =
  "onoff"|"brightness"|"color_temp"|"hs"|"xy"|"rgb"|"rgbw"|"rgbww"|"white"

class LightEntity extends Entity {
  domain: "light" = "light"                       // string-literal type
  supported_color_modes: Listing<ColorMode> = new {}
  min_color_temp_kelvin: Int(this > 0)? = null
  max_color_temp_kelvin: Int(this > 0)? = null
  effect_list: Listing<String>? = null

  // Derived capabilities — `hidden`, so they never leak into the JSON output.
  hidden dimmable: Boolean =
    supported_color_modes.toList().any((m) -> m != "onoff")
  hidden supportsColorTemp: Boolean =
    supported_color_modes.toList().contains("color_temp")
  hidden supportsColor: Boolean = ...
  hidden supportsEffects: Boolean = effect_list != null
}

class SensorEntity extends Entity {
  domain: "sensor" = "sensor"
  device_class: String? = null          // curated union in the real version
  state_class: ("measurement"|"total"|"total_increasing")? = null
  unit_of_measurement: String? = null
}

class ClimateEntity extends Entity {
  domain: "climate" = "climate"
  hvac_modes: Listing<"off"|"heat"|"cool"|"heat_cool"|"auto"|"dry"|"fan_only"> = new {}
  min_temp: Number? = null
  max_temp: Number? = null
}
```

On "do that for all the types": this schema has to be **hand-curated per domain** — HA's attribute shapes exist only in the developer docs, not in any machine-readable form the API exposes, so there's nothing to generate the schema itself from. That's fine in practice: you write the ~8–10 domains you actually use (light, sensor, switch, climate, cover, media_player, binary_sensor, …), each is 10–20 lines following its docs page, plus a `GenericEntity` fallback for domains you haven't typed yet. The schema is exactly the thing worth sharing as a package — it's HA-generic, not house-specific.

## 2. The generated dump (`dump.pkl`) — typed, dot-completable

`DataDump` would emit this instead of `dump.libsonnet`, dispatching on `domain` to pick the class and filling capabilities from `/api/states` attributes:

```pkl
class Bibliotek extends hass.Area {
  area_id = "bibliotek"
  area_name = "Bibliotek"

  taklys: hass.LightEntity = new {
    entity_id = "light.bibliotek_taklys"
    friendly_name = "Taklys bibliotek"
    supported_color_modes { "color_temp" }
    min_color_temp_kelvin = 2202
    max_color_temp_kelvin = 6535
  }
  leselampe: hass.LightEntity = new {
    entity_id = "light.bibliotek_leselampe"
    supported_color_modes { "brightness" }   // dims, no colour temp
  }
  temperatur: hass.SensorEntity = new { ... device_class = "temperature"; unit_of_measurement = "°C" }

  lights = List(taklys, leselampe)   // per-domain lists for iteration
  sensors = List(temperatur)
}

class Overetasje extends hass.Floor {
  floor_name = "Overetasje"
  bibliotek: Bibliotek = new {}
  stue: Stue = new {}
  areas = List(bibliotek, stue)
}

overetasje: Overetasje = new {}
```

So you get both access styles: `dump.overetasje.bibliotek.taklys` dot-completes in the editor *and is statically a `LightEntity`*, while `for (l in area.lights)` covers the comprehension style your current dashboards use. This mirrors what `home-codegen` already does for automations — same ethos, new target language.

## 3. Class-as-function components (`components.pkl`)

Each card class *is* the builder: hidden properties are the typed authoring surface, and the class derives the backend-facing generic shape from them via Pkl's late binding. Hidden props don't render, so the JSON output is unchanged and your Scala pipeline needs zero modification. The highlight — **constrained class types encode card/capability contracts**:

```pkl
abstract class Node {
  card: String
  params: Mapping<String, Any> = new {}
  children: Listing<Node> = new {}
}

/// Only accepts a light that can actually dim.
class BrightnessSlider extends Node {
  card = "slider"
  hidden entity: hass.LightEntity(dimmable)
  params {
    ["entity"] = entity.entity_id
    ["label"] = entity.friendly_name ?? entity.entity_id
    ["attribute"] = "brightness"
    ["min"] = 0
    ["max"] = 255
  }
}

/// Only a colour-temp-capable light; min/max come from ITS OWN metadata.
class ColorTempSlider extends Node {
  card = "slider"
  hidden entity: hass.LightEntity(supportsColorTemp)
  params {
    ["attribute"] = "color_temp_kelvin"
    ["min"] = entity.min_color_temp_kelvin
    ["max"] = entity.max_color_temp_kelvin
    ...
  }
}

class StateCard extends Node {
  card = "stateCard"
  hidden entity: hass.Entity
  hidden label: String? = null
  hidden value: String? = null    // optional JSONata override (the c.expr escape hatch)
  params {
    ["label"] = label ?? entity.friendly_name ?? entity.entity_id
    ["value"] = new Dynamic {
      transform = value ??
        #"$state & ($attr.unit_of_measurement ? " " & $attr.unit_of_measurement : "")"#
    }
  }
}
```

Note `#"..."#` custom-delimiter strings carry JSONata/Mustache text with zero escaping, and the current `Dashboard.validate` "declared inputs" check is now just… the type system.

## 4. The bigger dashboard (`overetasje.pkl`)

```pkl
import "components.pkl" as c
import "dump.pkl" as dump

/// Title, brightness slider per dimmable light, a colour-temp slider ONLY
/// where the light supports it, then the area's sensors.
function areaSection(area: hass.Area): c.Node = new c.Column {
  children {
    new c.SectionTitle { text = area.area_name }
    for (l in area.lights) {
      when (l.dimmable) { new c.BrightnessSlider { entity = l } }
      when (l.supportsColorTemp) { new c.ColorTempSlider { entity = l } }
    }
    for (s in area.sensors) { new c.StateCard { entity = s } }
  }
}

card: c.Node = new c.Column {
  children {
    new c.Row {
      children {
        new c.Button { label = "« Home"; action = c.navigate("dashboard") }
        new c.SectionTitle { text = dump.overetasje.floor_name }
      }
    }
    for (area in dump.overetasje.areas) { areaSection(area) }
    new c.StateCard {
      entity = dump.overetasje.stue.effekt     // typed dot-path, autocompletes
      label = "Strømforbruk stue"
      value = #"$state & " W""#
    }
  }
}
```

Evaluating this through `pkl-core` from Scala emitted the expected tree — e.g. taklys got both a brightness slider and a color-temp slider with `min: 2202, max: 6535` pulled from its own metadata, while leselampe correctly got only the brightness slider.

## 5. The error case — the reason to do all this

I then wrote a broken dashboard putting a `ColorTempSlider` on the brightness-only leselampe. The build fails with:

```
Type constraint `supportsColorTemp` violated.

66 | hidden entity: hass.LightEntity(supportsColorTemp)
                                     ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
at components#ColorTempSlider.entity (components.pkl)

6 | entity = dump.overetasje.bibliotek.leselampe
             ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
at broken#card.entity (broken.pkl)
```

It points at the contract *and* the offending dashboard line. In jsonnet this class of mistake ships silently and renders a slider bound to an attribute the light doesn't have.

Two honest caveats from the exercise: the per-area classes make the generated `dump.pkl` more verbose than the JSON blob (a non-issue — it's generated), and one thing the types still can't reach is the *inside* of JSONata strings — `value = #"$state & " W""#` is opaque to Pkl, so your runtime transform-compile check stays. Also note this supersedes part of the entity-card/JSONata ADR's "one generic entity card" framing — worth a dated `## Update —` if you adopt it.

191	  //   toggleTap        -> service call resolved from the entity's domain (default).

193	  //   openPopup(id)    -> open the surface registered under `id`.
194	  //   openPopup(node)  -> inline popup content; the backend hoists it to a surface.
195	  //   closePopup()     -> dismiss the open popup (drop a close button inside it).

199	  // openPopup:: is defined as a standalone builder further down. A surface is

203	  // arg is accepted-but-ignored so existing `closePopup('x')` call sites still

ASSISTANT  2026-07-02T20:05:54.468Z
==============================================================================
Done — the generic cards work in Pkl, and the `sliderSpec` pattern ports over with a nice upgrade: the same table now drives **three tiers of resolution** — explicit per-instance override → build-time lookup from the entity's domain → today's runtime JSONata `$lookup($domain)` for dynamic groups. Working code is in `scratchpad/pkl-spike3/`, evaluated end-to-end through pkl-core.

## The spec table — same shape as line 219, but typed

```pkl
class SliderSpec {
  action: String // "<domain>/<service>" the drag calls
  key: String    // service_data key the value rides on
  min: Int
  max: Int
  value: String  // the live position attribute
}

/// Add a domain by adding a row — no builder change, same as today. But now
/// TYPED: a row with a missing/misspelled field is a build error.
const sliderSpec: Mapping<String, SliderSpec> = new {
  ["light"] = new { action = "light/turn_on"; key = "brightness"; min = 1; max = 255; value = "brightness" }
  ["cover"] = new { action = "cover/set_cover_position"; key = "position"; min = 0; max = 100; value = "current_position" }
  ["fan"]   = new { action = "fan/set_percentage"; key = "percentage"; min = 0; max = 100; value = "percentage" }
}
```

## ONE generic Slider for all domains

```pkl
class Slider extends Node {
  card = "slider"
  hidden entity: hass.Entity(isDynamic || sliderSpec.containsKey(domain))
  hidden label: (String|Expr)? = null
  hidden min: Int? = null // per-instance overrides of the domain default
  hidden max: Int? = null

  hidden spec: SliderSpec? =
    if (entity.isDynamic) null else sliderSpec[entity.domain]

  // override -> build-time spec -> runtime $domain lookup (reactive = false, as today)
  function cfg(ov: Any?, get: (SliderSpec) -> Any): Any =
    if (ov != null) ov
    else if (spec != null) get.apply(spec)
    else new Expr { transform = sliderLookup(get); reactive = false }

  params {
    ["entity"] = entity.entity_id
    ["action"] = cfg(null, (s) -> s.action)
    ["key"]    = cfg(null, (s) -> s.key)
    ["min"]    = cfg(min, (s) -> s.min)
    ["max"]    = cfg(max, (s) -> s.max)
    ["value"] =
      if (spec != null) new Expr { transform = "$attr." + spec.value }
      else new Expr { transform = "$lookup($attr, " + sliderLookup((s) -> s.value) + ")" }
    ...
  }
}
```

The `sliderDomainMap`/`sliderLookup` helpers port almost verbatim (manifest the table as a JSONata object literal, wrap in `$lookup(..., $domain)`), so the dynamic path is derived from the **same table** — one place to add cover/fan/climate, exactly as today. The `EntityCard` got the same treatment: `value`/`secondary` accept the three forms (null → `$state` + auto-unit, string → `$attr.<name>` + unit, `expr(...)` verbatim), `exprOf` carries its `entityId` for cross-entity slots, and the default tap resolves from a `tapService` domain table with the `homeassistant/toggle` fallback.

## Usage and what comes out

```pkl
new c.Slider { entity = dump.overetasje.bibliotek.taklys }        // spec resolved at build
new c.Slider { entity = dump.overetasje.bibliotek.leselampe; min = 25 }  // override
new c.EntityCard { entity = dump.overetasje.bibliotek.temperatur }       // $state + unit
new c.Slider { entity = hass.SELF }                               // dynamic group case
```

The static light emits fully resolved config — `"action": "light/turn_on", "key": "brightness", "min": 1, "max": 255` as plain values, no runtime lookup needed anymore. The `hass.SELF` sentinel emits exactly today's mechanism:

```json
"action": { "transform": "$lookup({\"light\":\"light/turn_on\",\"cover\":\"cover/set_cover_position\",\"fan\":\"fan/set_percentage\"}, $domain)", "reactive": false },
"value":  { "transform": "$lookup($attr, $lookup({\"light\":\"brightness\",...}, $domain))" }
```

This respects your "prefer runtime mechanisms over build-time assumptions" principle where it *has* to hold (dynamic groups, where the entity is unknowable at build), while cashing in build-time knowledge where it's free (static entities). And misuse is caught: `new c.Slider { entity = <a sensor> }` fails the build with `Type constraint 'isDynamic || sliderSpec.containsKey(domain)' violated`, pointing at both the constraint in components.pkl and the offending dashboard line.

Two Pkl gotchas surfaced while building this, worth knowing for a real port: `override` is a reserved keyword (needs backticks or a rename), and module-level properties referenced from inside class bodies must be marked `const` — a mechanical annotation, and the error message tells you the fix.

So the earlier capability-specialized cards (`ColorTempSlider` etc.) aren't the required style — they're an *option* the type system opens up. The generic-card + domain-table model you have today carries over one-to-one, just with the table typed, the domain gate enforced at build time, and per-instance overrides kept.

# Jsonnet authoring setup — complete feature surface

All paths under `modules/fh-datastar-view/src/main/resources/dashboards/`. Line refs are `file:line`.

## 1. components.libsonnet — components/builders & backend coupling

**Value-expression helpers (display-field wrappers):**
- `expr(s)` — `components.libsonnet:39`. Wraps a JSONata expr over the card's own entity (`$state/$attr/$domain/$entity_id`); live, repaints on state change. Emits `{ transform: s }`.
- `exprOf(eo, s)` — `:47`. Like `expr` but binds the slot to a **different** entity (`{ entityId, transform }`); the card joins both entities' live-dependency sets. This is the multi-entity card mechanism.

- `labelSlot(eo,label)` — `:67`. String→literal, `c.expr`→live, null+`$self`→live friendly_name default, null+static→baked literal friendly_name. Note `$self` sentinel handling at `:78`.

- `exprOrAttr` `:94`, `entityOf` `:102`, `valueSlot` `:116`, `secondarySlot` `:125`.

**Tap/action descriptors (backend-coupled URL construction — all in jsonnet, backend holds no URL literals):**
- `defaultRoute` — `:137`. JSONata `$lookup` mapping domain→service (scene/script/button→_press/turn_on, else `homeassistant/toggle`), resolved per-entity at runtime.
- `serviceOnclick(route)` — `:146`. Builds `@post('/sse/action/<domain>/<service>/<entity_id>')`.
- `constOnclick` `:151`.

# fh-datastar-view — Scala architecture inventory (for adding Pkl alongside jsonnet)

All paths under `/home/kanper/Dropbox/dev/functional-home-assistant/`. Module root: `modules/fh-datastar-view/`.

The key design fact for your task: **the runtime model (`Dashboard`) is a plain circe-decoded case-class tree that knows nothing about jsonnet.** jsonnet only exists in the *build* layer as "source text → JSON". So Pkl is a matter of adding a second "source → JSON (+ import set)" evaluator and teaching discovery/entry-selection about a second extension. Below, every jsonnet-specific seam is flagged.

## 1. Model layer — `src/main/scala/fh/view/model/`

### `Dashboard.scala` (the whole model lives in one file)

**`Dashboard`** case class (lines 338-344):
- `cards: Map[String, CardDef]` — the shared named-template library.
- `card: LayoutNode` — root of the recursive layout tree.
- `theme: Theme = Theme()` (default empty).
- `surfaces: Map[String, Surface] = Map.empty` — popups/tab-panels keyed by id.
- `slug: String = "dashboard"` — route id (`/d/<slug>`); overridden at runtime from filename (see §2).
- No `tabs` field — tabs are modeled as surfaces (baked panels), not a top-level field.
- Derives `ConfiguredDecoder` (line 344). The circe `Configuration` is set at lines 54-57: `withDefaults`, discriminator key `"kind"`, constructor names lowercased. This discriminator drives `LayoutNode` and `Predicate` decoding.

**`Dashboard.validate`** (lines 357-441), returns `List[String]` (empty = valid):
- `checkRef` (363-379): every `card` reference resolves in `cards`; every *required* slot the `CardDef` declares is satisfied by an authored slot OR a backend-injected name. Extra slots ignored; only missing required flagged.
- `slotErrors` (383-395): each non-literal slot's `transform` must parse as JSONata (`Transform.parse`), else hard error. Uses `locateTransform` for a `file:line` hint.
- `chromeErrors` (425-... [13676 chars truncated]

# Implementation Plan: Pkl as a second dashboard-authoring language in `fh-datastar-view`

Jsonnet stays untouched as the primary track. Pkl is additive: `.pkl` entries discovered next to `.jsonnet` ones, dispatched by extension at a new `SourceEval` seam. Pkl library modules live in a new `lib/` subdirectory of the dashboards dir (this is how entries and libraries are distinguished — with jsonnet the `.libsonnet` extension did that job; with Pkl everything is `.pkl`, so directory convention replaces extension convention).

Scope corrections applied from the requirements (vs. the spike code): **`exprOf` is deferred** (skip-list item "exprOf multi-entity slots"), **no `$self`/DynamicEntity sentinel** (ADR 0003 deferred), **slider config is build-time only** (no runtime `$lookup($domain)` fallback), **no `class` slot on row/col**, **light is the only slider domain**. `hass.pkl` must be typed against what `DataDump` *actually fetches* (entity_id, friendly_name, id_hidden, area_id, floor_id, domain, and for lights `attributes.{color_mode, effect_list}`) — NOT the spike's richer `supported_color_modes` schema, which the dump does not carry.

## Approved Plan (edited by user):
# Pkl authoring track alongside jsonnet in fh-datastar-view

## Context

The Datastar dashboard DSL is authored in jsonnet today: untyped, no editor completion, sharing = copy files. Investigation (spikes verified in-process on this repo's JDK 21) showed Pkl gives compile-time checking (typed cards, capability constraints, carets pointing at both the contract and the offending dashboard line), LSP/IntelliJ completion, and a real package system — with a tiny integration surface: `org.pkl-lang:pkl-core:0.31.1` (3.3 MB, Java dep) evaluates a `.pkl` module to JSON text (`Evaluator.preconfigured().evaluateOutputText`), which feeds the existing circe pipeline unchanged.

**Goal:** add Pkl as an ADDITIONAL authoring language — `.pkl` dashboards discovered/served next to `.jsonnet` ones, a typed `dump.pkl` generated beside `dump.libsonnet`, theme parity — as a deliberately small MVP with an explicit skip-list to grow into full jsonnet parity. Each step below is sized for Opus 4.8 (medium thinking) to execute independently, with its own verification.

**Layout convention:** Pkl library modules live in `dashboards/lib/` (`hass.pkl`, `components.pkl`, `theme.pkl`, `tokens.pkl`, generated `dump.pkl`); top-level `*.pkl` files are dashboard entries (with jsonnet the `.libsonnet` extension made this distinction; Pkl has one extension, so directory convention replaces it). Discovery (`os.list`, non-recursive) never sees `lib/`.

**Working spike code to crib from:** `/tmp/claude-66815/-home-kanper-Dropbox-dev-functional-home-assistant/77f9768c-7277-4b0b-b4be-b7a1dd45abba/scratchpad/pkl-spike2` and `pkl-spike3` (may not survive reboots — the plan text is self-sufficient).

477	  test("literalLocator points a transform back at its jsonnet line") {
478	    val dir = os.temp.dir()
479	    os.write(
480	      dir / "dashboard.jsonnet",
481	      "local c = import 'x';\n" +
482	        "{ value: c.entityCard(p, transform='$round($number($state), 1)') }\n"
483	    )
484	    // The generated dump is skipped even if it contains the literal.
485	    os.write(dir / "dump.libsonnet", "{ x: '$round($number($state), 1)' }\n")
486	
487	    val locate = JsonnetBuild.literalLocator(
488	      Set(dir / "dashboard.jsonnet", dir / "dump.libsonnet")
489	    )
490	    assertEquals(
491	      locate("$round($number($state), 1)"),
492	      Some("dashboard.jsonnet:2")
493	    )
494	    assertEquals(locate("$nope($)"), None)
495	  }

1	// Design tokens — Home Assistant frontend theme variables.
2	// https://www.home-assistant.io/integrations/frontend/
3	//
4	// A theme is a map of `variable-name -> value`. The runtime injects each as a
5	// CSS custom property `--<variable-name>` on the dashboard root, and the
6	// component styles read them via `var(--<variable-name>)`. The names match HA's
7	// so an existing HA theme can be dropped in.
8	//
9	// `light` is the base palette; `dark` holds the overrides applied under
10	// `@media (prefers-color-scheme: dark)`, so the dashboard follows the browser's
11	// light/dark setting (the web standard) automatically. Override per dashboard,
12	// e.g. `theme: tokens.light + { 'primary-color': '#bada55' }`.
13	{
14	  light: {
15	    'primary-color': '#03a9f4',
16	    'accent-color': '#ff9800',
17	    'primary-background-color': '#fafafa',
18	    'secondary-background-color': '#e5e5e5',
19	    'card-background-color': '#ffffff',
20	    'primary-text-color': '#212121',
21	    'secondary-text-color': '#727272',
22	    // Text drawn on top of `primary-color` (e.g. button labels).
23	    'text-primary-color': '#ffffff',
24	    'disabled-text-color': '#bdbdbd',
25	    'divider-color': 'rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.12)',
26	    'error-color': '#db4437',
27	    'warning-color': '#ffa600',
28	    'success-color': '#43a047',
29	    'info-color': '#039be5',
30	    'ha-card-border-radius': '12px',
31	  },
32	
33	  // Only the tokens that differ in dark mode; the rest inherit from `light`.
34	  dark: {

15	/** Runtime phase entry point.
16	  *
17	  * Connects to Home Assistant, discovers every `*.jsonnet` dashboard entry in
18	  * the dashboards dir (slug = filename), evaluates each **in memory** into the
19	  * runtime model, seeds live state, and serves them with live Datastar updates.
20	  * Run via `fh-datastar-view/runMain fh.view.runtime.ServerApp` with
21	  * `SERVER`/`SECRET` set.
22	  */
23	object ServerApp extends IOApp {

29	    for {
30	      dashboardsDir <- pathFromEnv("DASHBOARDS_DIR", defaultDashboardsDir)
31	      bindHost <- Env[IO]
32	        .get("HOST")
33	        .map(_.flatMap(Host.fromString).getOrElse(host"0.0.0.0"))
34	      bindPort <- Env[IO]
35	        .get("PORT")

1	# Architecture Decision Records
2	
3	Short notes capturing a significant decision: its context, the options weighed,
4	and the outcome. Numbered sequentially. While the module's design is still in
5	flux (pre-v1), an ADR is kept current by appending a dated **`## Update —`**
6	section that records the new design and names the decision it supersedes (rather
7	than always minting a new ADR); each `Update` is the latest word on what it
8	touches.
9	
10	- [0001 — Entity card + per-slot value transforms via JSONata](0001-entity-card-and-value-transforms.md) (updated 2026-06-25b: `params` dissolved, `entity_id` is a magical slot; domain-aware slider)
11	- [0002 — Multiple dashboards, popup surfaces, and in-place navigation](0002-multi-dashboard-popups-and-navigation.md) (updated 2026-06-26: the `Mount` node is deleted — host HTML lives in templates; **2026-07-02: options A + B adopted** — `Surface` collapses to `(content, bakeInto, bakeAs, bakeIndex, defaultOpen)`, host derived via `Surface.hostId`, popups no longer stack, open/switch/close unify as `swapHost`, and the `#dashboard` frame + popup host move into `Theme.chrome` (backend holds zero frame HTML; the document shell stays in `Server.page()`))
12	- [0003 — Dynamic groups: live membership + per-entity card dispatch](0003-dynamic-groups.md) (partly superseded by 0004; updated 2026-06-25: query-filtered re-renders, presets dropped)
13	- [0004 — Label as a slot; AST (not JSONata) for queries; attribute memoization](0004-label-as-slot-and-predicate-engine.md) (updated 2026-06-25b: `params` gone, `entity_id` the magical inheritance root; literal/inherited/reactive slot model, identity-slot memoization)
14	- [0005 — Node-scoped UI state and the cookie persistence tier](0005-node-state-and-the-cookie-tier.md) (cookie = the only client store the server reads on the GET → flash-free first-paint restore via `bakeInto`/`bakeAs`; declared-`state` sugar deferred until a 3rd consumer)
15

[tool call: Write] {"file_path": "/home/kanper/Dropbox/dev/functional-home-assistant/docs/adr/0006-pkl-authoring-track.md", "content": "# 0006 — Pkl as a second authoring language (typed dashboards alongside jsonnet)\n\nDate: 2026-07-03. Status: **Accepted** (MVP shipped).\n\n## Context\n\nDashboards are authored in jsonnet: untyped, no editor completion beyond\ntop-level fields (a limitation `components.libsonnet` itself laments), and\nsharing a component library means copying `.libsonnet` files. An investigation\n(spikes run in-process against this repo's JDK) showed\n[Pkl](https://pkl-lang.org) offers what jsonnet structurally cannot:\n\n- **compile-time checking** — typed card classes, constrained types\n  (`hass.Entity(sliderSpec.containsKey(domain))` makes \"slider on a sensor\" a\n  build error whose carets point at both the contract and the offending\n  dashboard line);\n- **editor support** — official LSP, VS Code and IntelliJ plugins with\n  completion/diagnostics over classes AND over a *generated typed dump*\n  (`dump.entities.<key>` dot-completes as a `LightEntity`);\n- **a real package system** — versioned packages via `package://` imports, the\n  sharing story for the component library;\n- **a tiny integration surface** — `org.pkl-lang:pkl-core` (3.3 MB, plain Java\n  dep, JDK 17+) evaluates a module to JSON text that feeds the existing circe\n  pipeline unchanged.\n\n## Decision\n\nPkl is **additive**, not a replacement. Jsonnet remains the primary track; the\ntwo coexist in the... [5393 chars truncated]

77	  URLs, ids) use `{{{...}}}`. Jsonnet sources live in `src/main/resources/dashboards/`
78	  (`components.libsonnet`, `dashboard.jsonnet`); `dump.libsonnet` and `dashboard.json` are
79	  generated + gitignored.
80	- Interactivity uses the WS `call_service` command (added to `ha-api`'s `CommandPhase` +
81	  `HomeAssistantApi.callService`). `POST /sse/action/:domain/:service/:entityId` triggers a no-data
82	  service; the value-carrying variant `.../:entityId/:key/:value` builds `service_data` (the value
83	  rides in the URL path, since Datastar template-literal URL interpolation isn't confirmed in v1 —
84	  use `'.../key/' + $signal` concatenation client-side). The resulting state change flows back over
85	  the persistent SSE stream.
86	- Templates (`components.libsonnet`): `fhrow`/`fhcol` containers, `sectionTitle`, `stateCard`,
87	  `button`, `slider` — each declares its `inputs`, checked by `Dashboard.validate`. Builders return
88	  layout nodes referencing a template by name; new container/leaf kinds are added as a template +
89	  builder with no Scala change. Datastar attributes use **colon** syntax (`data-on:click`,
90	  `data-bind`, `data-signals`). `SlotSource.default` fills absent/null attributes (e.g. brightness
91	  when a light is off).
92	- Dynamic groups: a `LayoutNode.Dynamic` runs a simple property-query AST (`Predicate`:
93	  And/Or/Not/Cmp over `domain`/`state`/`attr:<name>`) against live state and renders each matching
94	  entity via the first `case` whose `when` matches (per-entity/per-domain template dispatch).
95	
96	### The sbt plugin glue

10	The `fh-datastar-view` module (a simpler HA frontend, ported from the TS prototype in
11	`../ha-frontend`) was implemented and verified live against the user's HA on 2026-06-19, then
12	**redesigned on 2026-06-20** (recursive layout + template-by-name + dynamic queries).
13	
14	The project is **pre-v1 alpha** (banner in root `README.md`) — breaking changes are taken freely.
15	
16	**Current architecture (post-redesign; transform-slots refactor 2026-06-23):** the build artifact is
17	`dashboard.json` = `{ cards: Map[name, {template, params, slots}], card: <recursive tree>, theme }`.
18	- `cards` is a SHARED Mustache library keyed by name (entityCard, button, slider, sectionTitle,
19	  fhrow/fhcol). `CardDef` declares typed **`params`** (static/injected) + **`slots`** (live) — replaced
20	  the old flat `inputs` list (2026-06-23). Cards are reused — NOT baked per entity.
21	- **A slot IS a transform** (2026-06-23): `SlotSource = { entity, transform = "$state", default,
22	  bypassUnavailable = false }`. The `attribute` field is GONE — selecting a value is the transform:
23	  `"$state"` shows state, `"$attr.brightness"` an attribute, `"$lookup(…, $domain)"` an identity value.
24	  Bindings: `$state`, `$attr` (attr object; numeric attrs stay numeric), `$domain`, `$entity_id`.
25	  One mechanism for live AND identity-derived values; NO separate "computed"
26	  concept. `EntityState` now carries its own `entityId` + a derived `domain` `val` (computed once at
27	  ingest from the fetched data, NOT recomputed per render — `Renderer.matches` and the transform both
28	  read `st.domain`). `Transform.run(expr, entity: EntityState)` reads `$domain`/`$entity_id` off the
29	  state. Binds via per-call `expr.createFrame()` + `fram... [29283 chars truncated]

ASSISTANT  2026-07-03T06:48:25.899Z
==============================================================================
All 8 plan steps are complete — the Pkl authoring track is live. `sbt dashboardServe` now serves `/d/pkl-demo` (authored in Pkl) alongside all six jsonnet dashboards, verified against your real HA instance.

**What was built**

- **`SourceEval` seam** (`fh/view/build/SourceEval.scala`): owns `Result(value, imports)` and dispatches by extension — `.jsonnet` → sjsonnet (unchanged), `.pkl` → new `PklBuild` (pkl-core 0.31.1, evaluated to JSON text → circe). Everything downstream (normalize/hoist/decode/validate/Renderer) is shared, untouched.
- **`dashboards/lib/`** — the Pkl library modules: `hass.pkl` (hand-written domain schema typed to what `DataDump` actually fetches, with `GenericEntity` fallback), `components.pkl` (cards as classes — Row/Column/SectionTitle/EntityCard/Button/Slider + `expr`/`serviceTap`/`navigate`, the typed `sliderSpec` table resolved at build time), `theme.pkl`/`tokens.pkl` (full parity port). Top-level `*.pkl` files are entries; a slug claimed by both languages is a clear startup error.
- **`PklDump`** generates a typed `lib/dump.pkl` from the same fetch as `dump.libsonnet` (both written on startup/build, both gitignored) — every entity a named, domain-typed property, areas with per-domain lists.
- **Docs**: ADR 0006 with the decision, tradeoffs, and the explicit skip-list toward jsonnet parity (tabs/ADR 0005, popups+hoist/ADR 0002, dynamic groups/ADR 0003, `exprOf`, runtime `$lookup` slider config, extra slider domains); ADR README index and CLAUDE.md updated.

**Verification**: `testFull` = 68 green (was 59), including a `BuildPhaseSuite`-mirror end-to-end test that runs the Pkl demo through the full pipeline (`validate == Nil`, slider `min`/`max` decoded as string literals — the one contract rule that silently breaks everything if violated). Live: real values render ("2167 W", the `$round` expr showing "237.3 V"), the slider is bound to `light.philips_lct001_light` with `min="1" max="255"` from the spec, tap onclick resolves through JSONata, editing `pkl-demo.pkl` hot-reloads in ~4s, and the jsonnet dashboards are unaffected.

Three Pkl gotchas surfaced during implementation beyond the planned ones, now recorded in ADR 0006: amending a null-defaulted `Listing` fails when forced (assign `= new Listing {...}`), a doc comment in an entry file (no `module` clause) illegally attaches to the first import, and `tokens = tokens.light` self-recurses (alias the import). Everything is uncommitted on `main` — say the word if you want it committed or split into commits per step.

134	/** A simple property-query AST evaluated at runtime against live entity state.

142	object Predicate:
143	  case class And(items: List[Predicate]) extends Predicate
144	  case class Or(items: List[Predicate]) extends Predicate
145	  case class Not(item: Predicate) extends Predicate
146	  case class Cmp(property: String, op: Op, value: Json) extends Predicate

577	  // entity, not a preset.
578	
579	  // ---- dynamic groups (the whole DSL, namespaced under `dynamic`) ----
580	  // A dynamic group renders one card PER live entity matching a `query`,
581	  // optionally dispatching the card per entity. The matched entity's
582	  // id/entity_id/label are auto-injected and EVERY slot is rebound to it (see
583	  // Renderer.renderCase) — so a case is built with the SAME leaf builders as a
584	  // static card, just passing `dynamic.matched` as the entity. That is why there
585	  // are no `dyn*` builders: `c.entityCard`/`c.button`/`c.slider` (+ presets)
586	  // serve both static and dynamic use.
587	  //
588	  // Usage (alias `local d = c.dynamic;`):
589	  //   d.group(d.whenState('on'), d.when([
590	  //     d.case(d.whenDomain('light'), c.slider(d.matched)),
591	  //   ], fallback=c.entityCard(d.matched, tap=c.toggleTap)))
592	  //   d.group(d.lowBattery(20), c.entityCard(d.matched))   // single card
593	  //
594	  // Self-reference via the named local `dyn` (not `self`/`$`), so the nested
595	  // result objects of when/group can still reach sibling helpers.
596	  dynamic::
597	    local dyn = {
598	      // ---- query predicates (the Predicate AST) ----
599	      cmp(property, op, value):: { kind: 'cmp', property: property, op: op, value: value },
600	      and(items):: { kind: 'and', items: items },
601	      or(items):: { kind: 'or', items: items },
602	      pnot(item):: { kind: 'not', item: item },
603	      // Matches every entity (domain is never literally this sentinel).
604	      always:: dyn.cmp('domain', 'ne', '__never__'),
605	      whenDomain(d):: dyn.cmp('domain', 'eq', d),
606	      whenState(s):: dyn.cmp('state', 'eq', s),
607	      whenDeviceClass(cls):: dyn.cmp('attr:device_class', 'eq', cls),
608	      // e.g. attrLessThan('battery_level', 20)
609	      attrLessThan(attr, value):: dyn.cmp('attr:' + attr, 'lt', value),
610	      stateLessThan(value):: dyn.cmp('state', 'lt', value),
611	      // Battery s... [2471 chars truncated]

ASSISTANT  2026-07-03T11:09:37.922Z
==============================================================================
The plan is written to `docs/plan-pkl-parity.md` — seven steps implementing the ADR 0006 skip-list, each sized for Opus 4.8 medium with its own verification command. The key structural insight it's built on: **steps 1–5 need zero Scala changes** — the `inlineSurfaces`/`@@NODE_ID@@` hoist and the Dashboard decoder are source-agnostic, so tabs, popups, and dynamic groups are purely a matter of emitting the same JSON from Pkl that the jsonnet builders emit (I verified every contract against `components.libsonnet` and `Dashboard.scala` line by line).

**The steps:**

1. **Small gaps** — `exprOf` (thread `entityId` through the slot builders), the `class` slot on row/col (authored as `cssClass` since `class` is a Pkl reserved word), cover/fan slider domains.
2. **Dynamic groups** — the biggest step: widen the layout hierarchy to `LayoutNode` with a `DynamicGroup` sibling of `Node`, a typed Predicate AST (misspelled ops become build errors), the `d.*` helpers, the `$self`/`hass.SELF` sentinel, and labelSlot's live friendly-name default.
3. **Runtime `$lookup($domain)` slider tier** — the spike3 three-tier design (override → build-time spec → runtime lookup), only reachable by `$self` entities; static sliders keep their build-resolved config.
4. **Popups/surfaces** — `SurfaceDef`, `inlineSurfaces` riding on nodes/taps, the `popup` card, `openPopup`/`openPopupInline`/`closePopup` (split into two named functions since Pkl can't union-dispatch string-vs-node), registered `surfaces`, popup CSS.
5. **Tabs** — the `tabs` card + `Tabs` class composing `@@NODE_ID@@`-referenced surfaces, cookie-persisting button onclicks, `Button.active`, a `pkl-tabs.pkl` demo, and the tabs CSS. (Found a stray `',` artifact in the jsonnet tabs template at line 455 — the plan explicitly says not to port that bug.)
6. **Infra (only Scala step)** — precise import graph via pkl-core's analyze API replacing the all-`*.pkl` watch superset (with fallback), `DASHBOARD_ENTRY` for BuildApp.
7. **Live verification + docs** — browser pass on popups/tabs/dynamic against live HA, ADR 0006 dated `## Update —` marking the skip-list done, CLAUDE.md tweak.

The risk list calls out the two things most likely to bite an executor: the step-2 hierarchy restructure rippling through every `children` amend, and `defaultOpen` needing to be emitted as null-not-false to keep the hoisted JSON byte-compatible with jsonnet's.

One note: I drafted this directly rather than via a Plan agent (the earlier attempt hit the session limit), but every contract in it comes from file reads I did this session, not memory. Want me to commit the plan doc to the `pkl` branch, or start executing step 1?

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - fh-datastar-view: two-phase dashboard (jsonnet/Pkl composition → JSON → circe decode → Mustache render + Datastar SSE patches); phase discipline (no live values baked at build).
   - Pkl: pkl-core 0.31.1 (`org.pkl-lang % pkl-core`, plain Java dep, JDK 17+, 3.3MB), `Evaluator.preconfigured().evaluateOutputText(ModuleSource.path(...))`, `output { renderer = new JsonRenderer { omitNullProperties = true } }`; classes with `hidden` typed props deriving output; constrained types (`hass.Entity(sliderSpec.containsKey(domain))`); `for`/`when` generators; `#"..."#` custom-delimiter strings; pkl:analyze importGraph (0.27+) for precise imports.
   - Backend JSON contract (verified in Dashboard.scala): nodes `{kind:"component", card, slots, children}` with circe discriminator `kind` (lowercased constructor names); SlotSource dual form — bare JSON string = literal (MUST be string, never number; `Decoder[String]` rejects numbers), object = `{entityId?, transform="$state", default?, bypassUnavailable=true, reactive=true}`; `CardDef{template, slots}`; `Theme{tokens, tokensDark, stylesheets, styles, chrome}` (chrome must contain `id="dashboard"`); Predicate JSON `{kind:"cmp",property,op,value}`/`{kind:"and"|"or",items}`/`{kind:"not",item}`, op ∈ eq|ne|lt|lte|gt|gte, property ∈ "domain"|"state"|"attr:<name>"; DynamicCase `{when, card, slots}` (no entity_id slot; injectedDynamic={id,entity_id}); Surface `{content,bakeInto,bakeAs,bakeIndex,defaultOpen}`, hostId = bakeInto+"_"+bakeAs else PopupHostId.
   - `@@NODE_ID@@` token + `inlineSurfaces` markers hoisted by source-agnostic `DashboardBuild.hoistInlineSurfaces` — tabs/popups need ZERO Scala changes from Pkl.
   - Pkl gotchas discovered: `override` and `class` are reserved words; module-level properties referenced from class bodies must be `const` (`const local` for helper functions); amending a null-defaulted Listing is a type error when forced (assign `= new Listing {...}`); `///` doc comments before imports in module-clause-less entries are rejected; import name shadowed by a property being defined self-recurses (stack overflow) — alias the import; Pkl evaluation is lazy (unforced fields don't error).
   - sbt 2.0, munit, scalafmt; `sbt dashboardServe`/`dashboardBuild` aliases; live reload via fs2 Watcher over Result.imports union.

13	## Contract rules (verified; same as the MVP plan)
14	
15	- Nodes: `{kind: "component", card, slots, children}`; dynamic groups:
16	  `{kind: "dynamic", query, cases}` — `kind` is the circe discriminator.
17	- Slots: bare string = literal (MUST be a string, never a number); object =
18	  `{entityId?, transform, default?, bypassUnavailable, reactive}`.
19	- Predicate JSON: `{kind:"cmp", property, op, value}` /
20	  `{kind:"and"|"or", items}` / `{kind:"not", item}`; `op` ∈
21	  `eq|ne|lt|lte|gt|gte`; `property` ∈ `"domain"|"state"|"attr:<name>"`.

23	  `injectedDynamic = {id, entity_id}` so validate accepts it).
24	- `@@NODE_ID@@` is a literal token the build-phase hoist splices
25	  (`DashboardBuild.NodeIdToken`); surfaces lift to
26	  `surfaces["<idBase>_<localKey>"]`; `Surface.hostId` =
27	  `{bakeInto}_{bakeAs}` else `Dashboard.PopupHostId`.
28	- Pkl gotchas: `class`/`override` reserved; `const` for module refs from class
29	  bodies; assign (don't amend) null-defaulted Listings; filter a Mapping via a
30	  for-generator (`new Mapping { for (k, v in m) { when (k != "x") { [k] = v } } }`).

## Summary

Executed **Step 1** of `docs/plan-pkl-parity.md` — the small parity gaps. No commits made.

### Changes

**`modules/fh-datastar-view/src/main/resources/dashboards/lib/components.pkl`**
1. `Expr` gained `entityId: String? = null`; added `function exprOf(eo: hass.Entity, s: String): Expr` that sets it. Threaded `entityId` through all three slot builders into the emitted `Slot`: `labelSlot` (merges the whole descriptor, mirroring jsonnet), `valueSlot`, and `secondarySlot`.
2. `Row` and `Column` gained `hidden cssClass: String? = null` (authoring name, since `class` is reserved), emitting slot key `"class"` only when non-null via `slots { when (cssClass != null) { ["class"] = cssClass!! } }`. Templates already carry the `{{#class}}` sections.
3. `sliderSpec` gained `["cover"]` (`cover/set_cover_position`, key `position`, 0..100, value `current_position`) and `["fan"]` (`fan/set_percentage`, key `percentage`, 0..100, value `percentage`).

**`modules/fh-datastar-view/src/test/scala/fh/view/build/PklBuildSuite.scala`**
Added a `probeComponent` helper (temp-dir fixture copying `hass.pkl` + `components.pkl`, decoding a probe's `node` as `LayoutNode.Component`) and three tests: exprOf threads `entityId = Some("sensor.power")` into the slot (plus a plain-`expr` control that stays `None`); a `Row` with `cssClass` emits the literal `class` slot (plus an absent-case control asserting no `class` slot); a `Slider` on a cover `GenericEntity` resolves the cover spec (action/key/min="0"/max="100" as string literals, value transform `$attr.current_position`). Ran `sbt scalafmt`.

My 3 new tests: **all green** (verified both in the full suite run — 11 passed — and in isolation — 3/3).

15	
16	**Current architecture (post-redesign; transform-slots refactor 2026-06-23):** the build artifact is
17	`dashboard.json` = `{ cards: Map[name, {template, params, slots}], card: <recursive tree>, theme }`.
18	- `cards` is a SHARED Mustache library keyed by name (entityCard, button, slider, sectionTitle,
19	  fhrow/fhcol). `CardDef` declares typed **`params`** (static/injected) + **`slots`** (live) — replaced
20	  the old flat `inputs` list (2026-06-23). Cards are reused — NOT baked per entity.
21	- **A slot IS a transform** (2026-06-23): `SlotSource = { entity, transform = "$state", default,
22	  bypassUnavailable = false }`. The `attribute` field is GONE — selecting a value is the transform:
23	  `"$state"` shows state, `"$attr.brightness"` an attribute, `"$lookup(…, $domain)"` an identity value.
24	  Bindings: `$state`, `$attr` (attr object; numeric attrs stay numeric), `$domain`, `$entity_id`.
25	  One mechanism for live AND identity-derived values; NO separate "computed"
26	  concept. `EntityState` now carries its own `entityId` + a derived `domain` `val` (computed once at
27	  ingest from the fetched data, NOT recomputed per render — `Renderer.matches` and the transform both
